And when he adds divorce to marriage, it occurs after marriage, such as when he says to a woman: 'If I marry you, you are divorced,' or 'Every woman I marry, she is divorced.' Al-Shafi'i said it does not occur due to his saying (peace be upon him): 'No divorce before marriage.' Our proof is that this is a disposition of an oath because of the presence of the condition and consequence. So for the validity of an oath, the existence of ownership at the present moment is not required, because the occurrence is at the time of the condition, and ownership is certain at that time. Before that, its effect is prohibition, and it is established with the one making the disposition. The hadith is interpreted as negating immediate divorce, and this interpretation is transmitted from the predecessors such as al-Sha'bi, al-Zuhri, and others. Translation: And when divorce is attributed to marriage, it occurs after marriage. For example, if he says to a foreign woman: 'If I marry you, you are divorced,' or 'Every woman I marry, she is divorced.' And Imam Shafi'i said that divorce does not occur, due to the saying of the Prophet (PBUH) 'No divorce before marriage,' meaning there is no divorce before marriage. And our proof is that this is a disposition of an oath due to the presence of condition and consequence. So for the validity of a disposition of an oath, the existence of ownership at present is not a condition, because divorce occurs at the time of the condition, and ownership is certain at the time of the condition. Before that, its effect is prohibition, and it is established with the one making the disposition. And the hadith is interpreted as negating immediate divorce, and this interpretation is transmitted from the predecessors like al-Sha'bi and al-Zuhri and others. Explanation: The issue is that if divorce is suspended on marriage, for example, to a foreign woman: 'If I marry you, you are divorced' or 'Every woman I marry, she is divorced,' then according to us, in this case, divorce occurs after marriage. And Imam Shafi'i said it will not occur. Imam Shafi'i's proof is the hadith of the Prophet (PBUH), i.e., there is no divorce before marriage. Abdullah ibn Amr ibn al-Aas narrated that he sent a marriage proposal to a woman, and her guardians refused to marry him, so he said: 'If I marry her, she is divorced thrice.' Then the Prophet (PBUH) was asked about this and he said: 'No divorce before marriage.' From this hadith, it is known that there is no divorce before marriage. Our proof is that suspending on a condition is a disposition of an oath from the swearer, because the condition and consequence are both present. And that is called ta'liq (suspension). As for the point that at the time of suspension the swearer does not own, the answer is that for the validity of an oath, it is not a condition that ownership be present at the time of suspension. Rather, it is necessary that ownership exists at the time of the occurrence of the consequence. And since here at the time of the condition, ownership certainly exists, therefore the occurrence of divorce (the consequence) will be realized. Before the existence of the condition, the effect of the oath is only prohibition, i.e., to refrain from the thing sworn upon. And this prohibition is established with the one making the disposition. So at that time, there is no need for a subject of divorce; rather, the responsibility of the swearer is sufficient. The answer to the hadith presented by Imam Shafi'i is that this hadith is interpreted as applying to immediate divorce. The summary is that the Prophet (PBUH) said that if divorce is given before marriage, it does not occur. Obviously, no one disagrees on this. The discussion is about whether suspending divorce on marriage is permissible or not. And the hadith does not clearly address this. Therefore, using this hadith as evidence is not correct. And interpreting this hadith as applying to immediate divorce is transmitted from the predecessors, such as Imam al-Sha'bi, Imam al-Zuhri, and others besides them. Benefit: The root of the disagreement between Hanafis and Shafi'is regarding suspension is that according to the Shafi'is, the existence of ownership at both times—the time of uttering the suspension and the time of the condition's occurrence—is a condition. According to the Hanafis, it is necessary that ownership exist at the time of the condition's occurrence; it is not necessary at the time of suspension.
Source pages p. 330

Commentary
This passage presents a complete inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and the Shafi'is regarding the validity of conditional divorce before marriage. The Hanafis (Abu Hanifa and his students) rule that if a man says to a foreign woman 'If I marry you, you are divorced' or 'Every woman I marry is divorced,' then upon marriage the divorce takes effect. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, arguing that there is no divorce before marriage based on the hadith 'La talaqa qabl al-nikah'. The Hanafi response is that this hadith refers only to immediate divorce (talaq munajjaz), not to suspended divorce (talaq mu'allaq). They argue that suspending divorce on a condition is an oath (yameen), and an oath does not require ownership at the time of utterance; it only requires ownership at the time the condition is fulfilled. The Hanafis support their position by citing that the hadith is interpreted as such by early authorities (salaf) like al-Sha'bi and al-Zuhri. The passage concludes by summarizing the root of the disagreement: Shafi'is require ownership at both the time of utterance and the time of the condition, while Hanafis only require ownership at the time of the condition's occurrence.

Key Terms
تعلیق (ta'liq): Suspending a legal consequence (e.g., divorce) on a future condition.
یمین (yameen): In this context, a conditional divorce is considered a type of oath, binding the swearer to a consequence.
طلاق منجز (talaq munajjaz): Immediate divorce not dependent on any condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the underlying legal nature of a conditional divorce before marriage that makes it valid?
A) It is a form of marriage contract.
B) It is considered an oath (yameen).
C) It is a type of delegated divorce.
D) It is valid because the man owns the woman at the time of utterance.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school validates conditional divorce before marriage by categorizing it as an oath, requiring ownership only at the time the condition is fulfilled, while the Shafi'i school rejects it based on a literal interpretation of the hadith 'No divorce before marriage'.

Suspending Divorce on Future Marriage: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Dispute about validity of suspending divorce on a future marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on suspending divorce on a future marriage, explain the Hanafi proof distinguishing absolute from suspended divorce, and compare it with the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
A suspended divorce before marriage is a valid oath taking effect upon marriage, not an absolute divorce.

This lesson examines a classic dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the validity of suspending divorce on a future marriage. While the Shafi'is nullify such statements based on the hadith 'La talaq qabl al-nikah', the Hanafis treat them as binding oaths that become effective when the marriage occurs. Understanding the Hanafi reasoning requires distinguishing between absolute and suspended divorce and recognizing the nature of oaths.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the Hanafi ruling: suspended divorce on a future marriage is valid and takes effect upon marriage. Recognize that it is treated as a yamin (oath).
2
Identify the Shafi'i position and their proof
State that Imam al-Shafi'i holds no divorce occurs, relying on the hadith 'La talaq qabl al-nikah' from Abdullah ibn Amr ibn al-As.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response
Break down the Hanafi rebuttal: the hadith applies only to absolute (munajjaz) divorce, not suspended (mu'allaq). This interpretation is from early authorities like Sha'bi and Zuhri.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Describe the practical consequence: under Hanafi, the wife becomes divorced immediately upon marriage; under Shafi'i, no divorce occurs.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Explain why the Hanafi position is mufta bihi: based on the nature of oaths and the distinction between absolute and suspended divorce.

تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر طلاق کو نکاح پر معلق کیا گیا مثلاً اجنبی عورت سے کہا: ان تزوجتك فانت طالق باكها كل امرأة اتزوجها فهي طالق تو ہمارے نزدیک اس صورت میں نکاح کے بعد طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی۔ اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ واقع نہیں ہوگی ۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل حدیث رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم ہے۔ یعنی نکاح سے پہلے طلاق نہیں ہے۔ عبد اللہ بن عمرو بن العاص سے روایت ہے کہ انہوں نے کسی عورت کو پیغام نکاح بھیجا۔ اس عورت کے اولیا نے ان کے ساتھ نکاح کرنے سے انکار کیا تو عبد اللہ بن عمرو بن العاص نے فرمایا ان نكحتها فهي طالق ثلاثاً پھر اس بارے میں رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم سے دریافت کیا گیا تو آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا لا طلاق قبل النكاح - اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ قبل النکاح طلاق نہیں ہے۔
ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ کسی شرط پر معلق کرنا حالف کی طرف سے تصرف یمین ہے۔ کیونکہ شرط اور جزاء دونوں موجود ہیں ۔ اور اسی کا نام تعلیق ہے۔ رہی یہ بات کہ تعلیق کے وقت حالف کی ملک نہیں ہے تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ صحت یمین کیلئے تعلیق کے وقت یعنی فی الحال ملک کا موجود ہونا شرط نہیں ۔ بلکہ ترتب جزا یعنی وقوع طلاق کے وقت ملک کا ہونا ضروری ہے۔ اور چونکہ یہاں وجود شرط کے وقت یقیناً ملک موجود ہے۔ اسلئے وقوع طلاق یعنی جزاء کا ترتب ہو جائے گا۔ اور وجود شرط سے پہلے یمین کا اثر صرف منع ہے۔ یعنی مخلوف سے رکنا۔ اور یہ منع متصرف یعنی حالف کے ساتھ قائم ہے۔ پس اس وقت محل طلاق کی کوئی حاجت نہیں بلکہ حالف کا ذمہ کافی ہے۔ امام شافعی کی پیش کردہ حدیث کا جواب یہ ہے کہ یہ حدیث طلاق منجز پر محمول ہے۔ حاصل یہ کہ آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ نکاح سے پہلے اگر طلاق دی جائے تو وہ طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی۔ ظاہر ہے کہ اس میں کسی کا اختلاف نہیں ہے۔ کلام تو اس بارے میں ہے کہ طلاق کو نکاح پر معلق کرنا جائز ہے یا نہیں۔ اور اس پر حدیث میں کوئی صراحت نہیں۔ لہذا اس حدیث کو استدل میں پیش کرنا درست نہیں ۔ اور اس حدیث کو طلاق منجز پر محمول کرنا اسلاف سے منقول ہے۔ مثلاً امام شعمی ، امام زہری اور ان دونوں کے علاوہ فوائد احناف و شوافع کے درمیان تعلیق کے سلسلہ میں منشاء اختلاف یہ ہے کہ شوافع کے نزدیک تکلم با تعلیق اور وجود شرط دونوں اوقات میں ملک کا پایا جانا شرط ہے۔ اور احناف کے نزدیک وجود شرط کے وقت ملک کا ہونا ضروری ہے۔ تعلیق کے وقت ضروری نہیں ۔ اگر طلاق کو شرط پر معلق کیا تو شرط کے بعد طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی
The Book of Divorce: Translation: And when divorce is attributed to marriage, then divorce will occur after marriage. For example, saying to a stranger woman: 'If I marry you, then you are divorced,' or saying: 'Every woman I marry, she is divorced.' And Imam Shafi'i said that divorce does not occur, due to the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'No divorce before marriage.' And our proof is that this is an act of an oath, due to the existence of condition and consequence. Therefore, for the validity of an oath, current ownership is not a condition, because the occurrence of divorce is at the time of the condition, and ownership is certain at the time of the condition. Before the condition, its effect is only prohibition, and that prohibition is attached to the person making the oath. And the hadith is interpreted as referring to absolute divorce, and this interpretation is transmitted from the predecessors, such as Sha'bi and Zuhri and others. Explanation: The issue is that if divorce is suspended on marriage, e.g., to a stranger: 'If I marry you, you are divorced' or 'Every woman I marry is divorced,' then according to us, divorce will occur after marriage. Imam Shafi'i said it does not occur. His proof is the hadith 'No divorce before marriage' from Abdullah ibn Amr ibn al-As. Our proof is that suspending on a condition is an act of an oath, because condition and consequence exist. As for the objection that ownership is not present at the time of suspension, the answer is that for validity of the oath, current ownership is not required; only ownership at the time of the condition is necessary. Since ownership certainly exists at the time of the condition, the consequence (divorce) occurs. Before the condition, the oath only prohibits (the person from the prohibited action). This prohibition is attached to the person making the oath, so there is no need for a place of divorce at that time; the person's obligation suffices. The hadith of the Prophet is interpreted as referring to absolute divorce, not suspended. The difference between Hanafis and Shafi'is is that Shafi'is require ownership at both the time of utterance and the time of condition, while Hanafis require ownership only at the time of condition. If divorce is suspended on a condition, it occurs after the condition.
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the validity of suspending divorce on a future marriage. The Hanafi position is that such a suspended divorce is valid and takes effect upon marriage, because it is considered a verbal oath (yamin) rather than an immediate divorce. The Hanafis argue that for an oath, current ownership of the wife is not necessary; it suffices that ownership exists at the time the condition is fulfilled. The Shafi'i position, led by Imam al-Shafi'i, is that no divorce occurs at all, relying on the hadith 'La talaq qabl al-nikah' (no divorce before marriage). The Hanafi response is that the hadith refers to absolute (munajjaz) divorce, not suspended (mu'allaq) divorce. This interpretation is attributed to early authorities like Sha'bi and Zuhri. The fundamental difference between the schools is that the Shafi'is require ownership both at the time of utterance and at the time of the condition, whereas the Hanafis require ownership only at the time of the condition. Thus, according to the Hanafis, if a man says to a woman he later marries, 'If I marry you, you are divorced,' the divorce takes effect immediately upon the marriage contract.

Key Terms
یمین (yamin): An oath; a verbal commitment that imposes a prohibition or obligation upon the speaker, here referring to a suspended divorce.
تعلیق (ta'liq): Suspending a legal consequence (here divorce) upon the occurrence of a future condition.
منجز (munajjaz): Absolute, immediate divorce; not suspended on any condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a man says to a stranger woman, 'If I marry you, you are divorced,' and later marries her, what is the ruling?
A) No divorce occurs because marriage does not exist at the time of utterance.
B) Divorce occurs immediately upon marriage because it is a valid suspended divorce.
C) The marriage is invalid due to the mention of divorce.
D) The woman must give consent for the divorce to take effect.

Key Takeaway
A suspended divorce before marriage is valid in the Hanafi school because it is treated as an oath, and the hadith 'La talaq qabl al-nikah' applies only to absolute divorces.

Talaq — Divorce

Suspending Divorce on a Condition: Validity and Proof
Ruling on suspended divorce for existing wife with proof and response to objection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on suspended divorce for an existing wife and explain the proof based on the continuance of ownership.

Core Idea
A suspended divorce is valid and occurs upon condition because ownership is present and presumed to continue.

When a husband says to his wife, 'If you enter the house, you are divorced,' what is the legal effect? The Hanafi school, in agreement with others, rules that divorce occurs upon fulfillment of the condition. This rests on a key principle: the marriage ownership exists at the time of utterance and is presumed to continue. In this lesson, we analyse the ruling, the proof, and the response to a potential objection.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is suspending divorce on a condition (talaq mu'allaq). The ruling is that divorce occurs upon fulfillment of the condition, and it is valid (sahih).
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is qiyas (analogy) to immediate divorce (munajjaz). The basis: marital ownership (milk) exists at the time of utterance and is presumed to continue.
The dalil is aqli (rational) based on istishab (presumption of continuity).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The presence of milk now, with the presumption of its continuance, makes the suspended divorce analogous to an immediate divorce at the time the condition occurs.
The analogous element (illa) is the existence of milk at the time of the ruling.
4
Note the potential objection and response
Objection: ownership might cease before condition (e.g., husband gives immediate divorce). Response: the default is continuity; mere possibility is ignored.
This is the principle of istishab al-hal.
5
Note the cross-madhhab agreement
The ruling itself is agreed upon by Hanafis and Shafi'is, though they differ on the nature of the statement (oath vs. immediate divorce).

And when he adds it to a condition, it occurs after the condition, such as saying to his wife: 'If you enter the house, you are divorced.' This is by agreement because ownership is present currently, and it is apparent that it will remain until the time of the condition, so it is valid as an oath or as an immediate divorce. Translation: And when divorce is attributed to a condition, then divorce will occur after the condition. For example, saying to his wife: 'If you enter your house, you are divorced.' This ruling is agreed upon because marital ownership is currently present, and it is apparent that it will continue until the time of the condition, so suspending it is valid as an oath or as an immediate divorce. Explanation: The issue is that if a man suspends his wife's divorce on entering the house, e.g., 'If you enter the house, you are divorced,' then after the condition (entering the house) divorce will occur. This ruling is by agreement. The proof is that the suspended divorce, at the time of the condition, becomes like an immediate divorce. This is an answer to a question: It is accepted that when ownership exists, divorce occurs after the condition, but before the condition, there is a possibility that ownership may cease (e.g., he might give an immediate divorce before the condition). So it might be argued that due to this probability, his oath should not be valid. The answer is that currently ownership exists, and the prevailing presumption is that it will remain until the condition, because the original state of any established thing is its continuance, especially marriage which is for life. Therefore, the hypothetical possibility of loss of ownership is not considered. Thus, since ownership is present and likely to continue, his suspended words are valid as an oath according to us, and as an immediate divorce according to Imam Shafi'i. The author of Hidayah indicated this difference by saying 'as an oath or as an immediate divorce'. The difference is that in 'If you enter the house, you are divorced,' Imam Shafi'i says that at the time of utterance, the intention was to effect divorce, so the suspension is on the occurrence of divorce, not on the effect. According to us, at the time of utterance, it is only an oath; at the fulfillment of the condition, the divorce is realized, as if the husband said 'you are divorced' at the time of entering. Details are in books of usul al-fiqh. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding suspending divorce on a condition when the wife is already married. The ruling is that if a husband says to his wife, 'If you enter the house, you are divorced,' then divorce occurs upon her entering the house. This is agreed upon by all schools. The reasoning is that ownership (the marital bond) exists at the time of the statement and is presumed to continue until the condition is fulfilled. There is a potential objection: what if the husband divorces his wife before she enters the house, thereby ending ownership? The Hanafi response is that the default is continuity, and mere possibility does not invalidate the oath. The author notes a subtle difference between the Hanafis and Shafi'is: The Hanafis consider the suspended statement as a mere oath (yamin) at the time of utterance, with the divorce taking effect only when the condition is met (like saying 'you are divorced' at that moment). The Shafi'is consider it as an immediate divorce that is suspended in its effect, meaning the intention to divorce is present from the start. This difference is explored in works of usul al-fiqh.

Key Terms
یمینا او ایقاعا (yaminan aw iqa'an): Either as an oath (yamin) or as an immediate pronouncement (iqa'); both are valid because ownership is present and presumed to continue.
ملک (milk): Marital ownership (the right of the husband over the wife that allows divorce).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A suspended divorce for an existing wife is valid and takes effect upon condition because marital ownership is present and presumed to continue; the Hanafi school treats the utterance as an oath until the condition is met.

The Nature of the Suspended Statement: Oath vs. Immediate Divorce
Difference between Hanafi and Shafi'i on nature of conditional divorce statement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi view that the suspended statement is an oath (yamin) from the Shafi'i view that it is an immediate divorce (iqa'), and explain the practical implications.

Core Idea
Hanafis treat the conditional divorce as an oath until the condition; Shafi'is treat it as a suspended divorce from the start.

While all schools agree that a conditional divorce takes effect upon fulfillment of the condition, they differ on the nature of the husband's statement at the moment he utters it. The Hanafis consider it a mere oath (yamin) that becomes divorce only when the condition occurs. The Shafi'is consider it an immediate pronouncement of divorce that is suspended in effect. This difference, though subtle, has implications for related rulings such as revocation and expiation. In this lesson, we explore both views and their foundations.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
At the time of utterance, the statement is an oath (yamin). The divorce (iqa') occurs only upon fulfillment of the condition, as if the husband said 'you are divorced' at that moment.
2
State the Shafi'i position
At the time of utterance, the statement is an immediate divorce (iqa') that is suspended in its effect. The divorce is already intended from the start, but its occurrence is tied to the condition.
3
Identify the legal consequence
For Hanafis, since it is an oath, the husband can revoke or expiate before the condition; for Shafi'is, the divorce is already in effect and cannot be revoked.
This is a key practical difference.
4
Analyse the proof for each view
Hanafi proof: The literal wording includes 'if', indicating suspension; the intention is to make an oath, not to divorce immediately. Shafi'i proof: The words 'you are divorced' are a direct pronouncement; the condition only delays the effect, not the pronouncement itself.
Both rely on textual and contextual evidence.
5
Note the agreement on the final outcome
Both schools agree that if the condition is fulfilled, divorce occurs. The difference is only in the classification of the utterance.

الملک قائم فى الحال والظاهر بقاءه الى وقت وجود الشرط فيصح يمينا او ايقاعا ترجمہ اور جب طلاق کو شرط کی جانب منسوب کیا تو طلاق شرط کے بعد واقع ہوگی۔ مثلاً اپنی بیوی سے کہے اگر تو اپنے گھر میں داخل ہوئی تو تو طالقہ ہے۔ اور یہ (حکم) متفق علیہ ہے کیونکہ ملک نکاح فی الحال موجود ہے۔ اور ظاہر اس کی بقاء ہے وجو د شرط کے وقت تک پس یمینا یا ایقاعاً ( اس کا معلق کرنا ) صحیح ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی مرد نے اپنی بیوی کی طلاق کو دخول دار پر معلق کر دیا۔ مثلاً کہا ان دخلت الدار فانت طالق تو وجود شرط یعنی دخول دار کے بعد طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی اور یہ حکم بالا تفاق ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ معلق بالشرط وجو د شرط کے وقت منجز
کے مانند ہوتا ہے۔ لانَّ الملک قائم سے ایک سوال کا جواب ہے۔ سوال یہ ہے کہ یہ بات تو تسلیم ہے کہ جب ملک موجود ہو تو شرط کے بعد طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی ۔ مگر وجود شرط سے پہلے ۔ اس ملک کے زائل ہونے کا احتمال ہے بایں طور کہ یہ شخص وجود شرط سے پہلے طلاق منجز دے دے۔ پس مناسب یہ ہے کہ زوال ملک کے احتمال کی وجہ سے اس کی یمین بالکل صحیح نہ ہو۔ جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ فی الحال تو ملک موجود ہے۔ اور آئندہ کے بارے میں غالب گمان یہ ہے کہ وجود شرط کے وقت تک ملک باقی رہے گی۔ کیونکہ اصل ہر ثابت شدہ چیز میں یہی ہے کہ وہ ہمیشہ باقی رہے۔ خصوصاً نکاح جوزندگی بھر کیلئے کیا جاتا ہے۔ لہذاز وال ملت کے متوهم احتمال کی طرف کوئی توجہ نہیں کی جائے گی۔ پس جب یہ ثابت ہو گیا کہ فی الحال بھی ملک موجود ہے اور اغلب بھی یہی ہے کہ ملک باقی رہے گی۔ تو اس کا کلام معلق ہمارے نزدیک یمبین بن کر صحیح ہو گا۔ اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک ایقاع طلاق بن کر صحیح ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے یمینا اور ایقاعا فرما کر اختلاف کی طرف اشارہ کیا ہے۔ اضراب یہ ہے اس کی رات میں مثلاً ان دخلت الدار فانت طالق میں امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ تکلم کے وقت طلاق واقع کرنا متفق ہو گیا۔ لہذا دخول دار پر ایقاع معلق نہیں بلکہ وقوع طلاق معلق ہے۔ اور ہمارے نزدیک تکلم کے وقت اس کا کلام صرف یمین ہے۔ وجود شرط کے ایقاع طلاق متحقق ہو گا۔ گویا دخول زار کے وقت شوہر نے انت طالق کہا۔ تفصیل اصول فقہ کی کتابوں میں موجود ہے۔ وہاں مطالعہ کر لیا جائے ۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب
And when he adds it to a condition, it occurs after the condition, such as saying to his wife: 'If you enter the house, you are divorced.' This is by agreement because ownership is present currently, and it is apparent that it will remain until the time of the condition, so it is valid as an oath or as an immediate divorce. Translation: And when divorce is attributed to a condition, then divorce will occur after the condition. For example, saying to his wife: 'If you enter your house, you are divorced.' This ruling is agreed upon because marital ownership is currently present, and it is apparent that it will continue until the time of the condition, so suspending it is valid as an oath or as an immediate divorce. Explanation: The issue is that if a man suspends his wife's divorce on entering the house, e.g., 'If you enter the house, you are divorced,' then after the condition (entering the house) divorce will occur. This ruling is by agreement. The proof is that the suspended divorce, at the time of the condition, becomes like an immediate divorce. This is an answer to a question: It is accepted that when ownership exists, divorce occurs after the condition, but before the condition, there is a possibility that ownership may cease (e.g., he might give an immediate divorce before the condition). So it might be argued that due to this probability, his oath should not be valid. The answer is that currently ownership exists, and the prevailing presumption is that it will remain until the condition, because the original state of any established thing is its continuance, especially marriage which is for life. Therefore, the hypothetical possibility of loss of ownership is not considered. Thus, since ownership is present and likely to continue, his suspended words are valid as an oath according to us, and as an immediate divorce according to Imam Shafi'i. The author of Hidayah indicated this difference by saying 'as an oath or as an immediate divorce'. The difference is that in 'If you enter the house, you are divorced,' Imam Shafi'i says that at the time of utterance, the intention was to effect divorce, so the suspension is on the occurrence of divorce, not on the effect. According to us, at the time of utterance, it is only an oath; at the fulfillment of the condition, the divorce is realized, as if the husband said 'you are divorced' at the time of entering. Details are in books of usul al-fiqh. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding suspending divorce on a condition when the wife is already married. The ruling is that if a husband says to his wife, 'If you enter the house, you are divorced,' then divorce occurs upon her entering the house. This is agreed upon by all schools. The reasoning is that ownership (the marital bond) exists at the time of the statement and is presumed to continue until the condition is fulfilled. There is a potential objection: what if the husband divorces his wife before she enters the house, thereby ending ownership? The Hanafi response is that the default is continuity, and mere possibility does not invalidate the oath. The author notes a subtle difference between the Hanafis and Shafi'is: The Hanafis consider the suspended statement as a mere oath (yamin) at the time of utterance, with the divorce taking effect only when the condition is met (like saying 'you are divorced' at that moment). The Shafi'is consider it as an immediate divorce that is suspended in its effect, meaning the intention to divorce is present from the start. This difference is explored in works of usul al-fiqh.

Key Terms
یمینا او ایقاعا (yaminan aw iqa'an): Either as an oath (yamin) or as an immediate pronouncement (iqa'); both are valid because ownership is present and presumed to continue.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) A mere oath (yamin).
B) An immediate divorce (iqa') whose effect is suspended.
C) A conditional promise that requires renewal.
D) An invalid statement because it is conditional.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi and Shafi'i schools differ on whether a conditional divorce statement is an oath or an immediate divorce at utterance, with practical consequences for revocation and expiation.

General Rule: Valid Addition of Divorce Requires Current or Prospective Ownership
General rule for valid suspended divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions for valid attribution of divorce and apply the rule to determine the validity of a suspended divorce.

Core Idea
Divorce attribution is valid only with current ownership or a clear cause of ownership — the oath must be realistically deterrent.

This lesson presents a foundational qa'idah kulliyyah (general rule) from the Hanafi school regarding the validity of suspended divorce (ta'liq al-talaq). The rule clarifies that a husband cannot validly divorce a woman he does not own, unless he links the divorce to a future event that would cause ownership, such as marriage. Understanding this rule is essential for determining when a suspended divorce takes effect.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two valid scenarios
The rule states only two cases: either the husband currently owns the wife at the time of the statement, or he attributes the divorce to a cause of ownership (e.g., future marriage).
Current ownership means the wife is already married to him. Cause of ownership means a future event that will create marital ownership.
2
Understand the rationale
The ‘illa (effective cause) is that the consequence (divorce) must be apparently realizable to serve as a deterrent, fulfilling the meaning of an oath – strength and manifestation.
Without a realistic possibility, the oath would not be frightening and would lack its purpose.
3
Apply the equivalency
Attribution to the cause of ownership is treated like attribution to ownership itself because the consequence becomes apparent at the time the cause occurs (e.g., upon marriage, the divorce becomes effective immediately).
This means a suspended divorce linked to future marriage is valid even before the marriage takes place.
4
Test with examples
Apply the rule to various statements: classify as valid if there is current ownership or a clear cause of ownership; otherwise invalid.
For instance, 'If my current wife travels, she is divorced' is valid (current ownership). 'If I marry you, you are divorced' is valid (cause of ownership). 'If my neighbor enters, she is divorced' is invalid (no ownership relation).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قاعدہ کلیہ
ولا تصح اضافة الطلاق الا ان يكون الحالف مالكا او يضيفه الى ملك لأن الجزاء لابدان يكون ظاهرا ليكون مخيفا فيتحقق معنى اليمين وهو القوة والظهور باحد هذين والاضافة الى سبب الملك بمنزلة الاضافة اليه لانه ظاهر عند سببه
ترجمہ اور طلاق کی نسبت کرنا صحیح نہیں مگر یہ کہ قسم کھانے والا ( بالفعل ) مالک ہو یا طلاق ملک کی طرف منسوب کرے۔ کیونکہ جزاء کے واسطے غالب الوجود ہونا ضروری ہے۔ تاکہ وہ ڈرانے والا ہو جائے۔ پس یمین کے معنی متحقق ہو جائیں گے۔ اور وہ قوت ہے اور ظہور قوت ان دونوں میں سے ایک کے ذریعہ ہوگا اور ملک کے سبب کی طرف نسبت کرنا ملک کی طرف نسبت کرنے کے مرتبہ میں ہے۔ اسلئے کہ جزاء ظاہر ہوگی سبب ملک کے وقت ۔
General rule: The attribution of divorce is not valid unless the person swearing is (currently) the owner or he attributes it to ownership. Because the consequence must be apparently existent to be frightening, so the meaning of oath (which is strength and manifestation) is realized by one of these two. And attribution to the cause of ownership is like attribution to ownership itself, because it becomes apparent at the time of its cause.
Source pages p. 332

Commentary
This passage is a general rule (qa'idah kulliyyah) that sets the conditions for the valid attribution (idafah) of divorce. The rule states that for a divorce to be validly attributed (i.e., suspended on a future event), either (1) the husband must currently own the wife (i.e., she is his wife at the time of the statement), or (2) he must attribute the divorce to a cause of ownership (such as marriage, which is a cause of acquiring ownership). The reason is that the consequence (divorce) must be apparently likely to occur so that the statement serves as a deterrent, which is the purpose of an oath. The meaning of oath is strength and manifestation, and this is achieved either by current ownership or by linking to a cause that will bring ownership. Attributing to the cause of ownership (e.g., saying 'if I marry you') is equivalent to attributing to ownership itself because the consequence becomes apparent at the time the cause occurs (i.e., when the marriage is contracted).

Key Terms
اضافة الطلاق (idafat al-talaq): Attributing or linking divorce to a future event or condition, i.e., suspended divorce (ta'liq).
سبب الملك (sabab al-milk): A cause that leads to ownership, such as marriage (nikah) which is a cause for acquiring marital ownership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following suspended divorce statements is valid according to the Hanafi general rule?
A) A man says to his current wife: 'If my mother visits, you are divorced.'
B) A man says to a female stranger: 'If I marry you, you are divorced.'
C) A man says to a female stranger: 'If you enter this house, you are divorced.'
D) Both A and B are valid.

Key Takeaway
The validity of a suspended divorce depends on the presence of actual ownership or a clear link to a future cause of ownership.

Suspended Divorce as Oath: The Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute
Ruling on suspended divorce and the dispute over its legal nature

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the nature of suspended divorce (ta'liq) and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument, identifying the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
A suspended divorce is an oath (yamin) at utterance, not an immediate execution, because ownership is presumed to continue.

When a husband says 'If you enter the house, you are divorced,' is he swearing an oath or actually divorcing? The schools differ. This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling that such a statement is a valid oath (yamin) that becomes a divorce only upon the condition, and the Shafi'i view that it is an immediate execution (iqa') with suspended effect. The debate hinges on the principle of istishab—the presumption of continuity of ownership.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify how the Hanafi school classifies the statement at the moment of utterance: it is a yamin (oath), not an iqa' (execution). Divorce occurs only when the condition is fulfilled.
The key distinction is between the nature of the utterance and the occurrence of the divorce.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i considers the same statement as an iqa' (execution) at the time of utterance; the divorce itself is suspended, but the nature is already that of an execution.
For Shafi'i, the speaker intends to execute divorce at the moment of speaking, even if it takes effect later.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i argument is based on the literal wording: the husband says 'you are divorced,' which is an immediate declaration. The conditional clause suspends the occurrence but not the nature of the statement.
They argue that ownership at utterance is sufficient to make the statement an iqa'.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response invokes istishab: ownership exists now and is presumed to continue. The possibility of ownership ending before the condition (e.g., by an immediate divorce) is merely speculative and does not invalidate the ta'liq. Therefore, the statement is an oath valid at utterance.
The Hanafi position is that at the moment of speech, the condition is not yet met, so the divorce cannot be considered executed; hence it is an oath.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if the husband gives a final divorce before the condition, under Hanafi the suspended divorce is nullified (the oath is broken); under Shafi'i, the divorce would have already occurred at the time of the first statement.
This difference can affect whether the wife is divorced once or twice, etc.

The ownership exists in the present and apparent is its continuity until the time of the condition's existence, so it is valid as an oath or as an execution. Translation: And when divorce is attributed to the side of the condition, then divorce will occur after the condition. For example, saying to his wife: 'If you enter your house, you are divorced.' And this (ruling) is agreed upon because the ownership of marriage exists in the present, and its continuity is apparent until the time of the condition's existence. So suspending it as an oath or execution is valid. Explanation: The issue is that if a man suspends his wife's divorce on entering the house, e.g., said 'If you enter the house, you are divorced,' then upon the existence of the condition, i.e., entering the house, divorce will occur. And this ruling is unanimous. The proof is that the suspended-with-condition, at the time of condition's existence, is like the immediate. Because 'the ownership exists' is an answer to a question. The question is: It is accepted that when ownership exists, divorce will occur after the condition. But before the condition's existence, there is a possibility of this ownership ceasing, e.g., this person might give an immediate divorce before the condition. So it would be appropriate that due to the possibility of ownership ceasing, his oath (yamin) is not valid at all. The gist of the answer is that ownership exists in the present, and about the future, the dominant assumption is that ownership will remain until the condition exists. Because the principle in every established thing is that it remains forever. Especially marriage, which is done for a lifetime. Therefore, no attention is paid to the weak possibility of ownership ceasing. So when it is established that ownership exists now and most likely will remain, then his suspended statement is valid according to us as an oath (yamin). And according to Imam Shafi'i, it is valid as an execution of divorce (iqa'). The author of Hidayah indicated the difference by saying 'yaminan or iqa'an'. The objection is that in his statement, e.g., 'If you enter the house, you are divorced,' Imam Shafi'i says that at the time of speech, executing divorce was intended, so the execution is not suspended on entry, rather the occurrence of divorce is suspended. And according to us, at the time of speech, his statement is only an oath; at the condition's existence, the execution of divorce is realized, as if at the time of entry the husband said 'you are divorced.' Details are in usul al-fiqh books. And Allah knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 332

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya explains the ruling on suspended divorce (ta'liq al-talaq). The author begins by stating a base ruling from al-Hidayah: if a husband says to his wife 'If you enter the house, you are divorced,' the divorce occurs upon the fulfillment of the condition. This ruling is agreed upon (muttafaq 'alayh) between the schools because the husband owns the right to divorce at the time of utterance, and ownership is presumed to continue (istishab) until the condition is met. The commentary then addresses a potential objection: what if the husband divorces his wife before the condition? The answer uses the principle of istishab—ownership is present now and is likely to remain, as marriage is contracted for life. Hence, the ta'liq is valid. The passage then highlights a dispute: according to the Hanafi school, the statement is an oath (yamin) at the time of utterance, and divorce occurs only upon the condition (it is an iqa' later). According to Imam al-Shafi'i, the statement itself is an execution (iqa') of divorce, but the occurrence of divorce is suspended on the condition. The practical difference is that under Hanafi law, if the husband gives a final divorce before the condition, the suspended divorce is nullified (the oath is broken), while under Shafi'i, the divorce would have already taken effect. The author refers to usul al-fiqh for details.

Key Terms
یمین (yamin): An oath; a statement that does not effect divorce immediately but creates a binding promise that divorce will occur upon condition.
ایقاع (iqa'): Execution; a direct legal act that effects a change immediately or upon fulfillment of a condition.
معلق (mu'allaq): Suspended; a statement whose legal effect is contingent upon a future condition.
شرط (shart): Condition; a future event upon which the divorce is made contingent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when a husband says to his wife 'If you enter the house, you are divorced,' what is the legal nature of this statement at the time of utterance?
A) It is an immediate divorce (iqa').
B) It is an oath (yamin) that becomes an execution upon condition.
C) It is invalid because ownership might cease.
D) It is a recommendation (sunnah).

Key Takeaway
Suspended divorce is valid as an oath (yamin) under Hanafi; the actual divorce occurs only upon condition fulfillment, following the principle of istishab.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
8 min
General Rule for Valid Suspended Divorce (Ta'liq al-Talaq)
States the general rule for valid suspended divorce and applies it to a specific case.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions for a valid suspended divorce (ta'liq al-talaq) and apply them to determine the occurrence of divorce in a given scenario.

Core Idea
A suspended divorce is valid only if at utterance the husband owns the right or links it to future ownership.

This passage from al-Hidayah establishes a foundational rule for suspended divorce (ta'liq al-talaq). The rule clarifies that simply attaching divorce to a condition is not enough; the speaker must have a legal connection to the right to divorce at the time of speaking. This lesson unpacks the two conditions and applies them to a common scenario involving a non-marriageable woman.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conditions for validity
Read the first part of the passage: the swearer must either (a) currently own the right to divorce (be the husband) or (b) attribute the divorce to future ownership (e.g., linking it to the cause of ownership such as marriage). Note that both are alternatives.
The second condition 'attribution to the cause of ownership' is equivalent to attribution to ownership itself.
2
Understand the rationale
The passage explains that the consequence (divorce) must be likely to occur to instill fear, fulfilling the meaning of an oath (strength and manifestation). This rationale supports why ownership or a clear link to future ownership is required.
If the divorce is not likely to occur, the oath loses its purpose.
3
Apply to the example
Consider the case where a man says to a non-marriageable woman (ajnabiyyah): 'If you enter the house, you are divorced.' He later marries her, and she enters. Determine if divorce occurs by checking the two conditions.
At the time of utterance, he was not the owner (she was not his wife) and he did not attribute to ownership (no 'if I marry you'). Therefore, neither condition is met.
4
Formulate the ruling
Conclude that divorce does not occur. The suspended divorce is invalid because the swearer lacked the required connection to the right to divorce at the time of utterance.
This shows the practical consequence of the rule.

General rule: And attaching divorce is not valid unless the swearer is an owner (currently) or he attributes it to ownership. Because the consequence must be predominantly present to be frightening, so the meaning of oath is realized, which is strength and manifestation through one of these two. And attribution to the cause of ownership is like attribution to ownership itself, because it is apparent at the time of its cause. Translation: And attaching divorce is not correct unless the swearer is (actually) an owner or he attributes divorce to ownership. Because the consequence must be predominantly existent so that it becomes frightening. Thus the meaning of oath is realized, which is strength, and the manifestation of strength will be through one of these two: either the swearer is actually an owner or it is attributed to ownership. And attributing to the cause of ownership is of the same rank as attributing to ownership, because the consequence becomes apparent at the time of the cause of ownership. Explanation: In this sentence, the author (of al-Hidayah) has stated a rule. The rule is that attaching divorce to a condition is valid only when the swearer is actually the owner of the thing upon which the condition is placed. For example, saying to his wife: 'If you enter the house, you are divorced,' or he attributes divorce to his ownership, e.g., said: 'If I marry you, you are divorced.' The proof is that the consequence must be predominantly existent so that through the occurrence of the consequence the addressee can be frightened, and the meaning of oath is realized. The meaning of oath is strength, and the manifestation of strength will be through one of these two matters: either the swearer is actually an owner, or attribution has been made to ownership. And attribution to the cause of ownership is like attribution to ownership itself. For example, 'If I buy you, you are free,' 'If I own you, you are free' are of the same rank. (From 'Inayah)
He said to a non-marriageable woman: 'If you enter the house, you are divorced,' then he married her, then she entered the house, divorce does not occur. So if he said to a non-marriageable woman: 'If you enter the house, you are divorced,' then he married her, then she entered the house, divorce will not occur because the swearer is not an owner, and he did not attribute it to ownership or its cause, while one of them is necessary. Explanation: The issue is that if a man said to a non-marriageable woman: 'If you enter the house, you are divorced,' then that man married that woman, after which that woman entered the house, then in this case divorce will not occur. This issue is derived from the principles of the preceding. The proof is that the swearer is neither the owner of the right to divorce nor has he attributed the divorce to ownership or its cause, while for attaching divorce one of these two is necessary.
Source pages p. 332

Commentary
This passage presents a general rule (qaidah kulliyyah) from al-Hidayah regarding the validity of suspending divorce (ta'liq al-talaq). The rule states that attaching divorce to a condition is valid only if one of two conditions is met: (1) the swearer (al-halif) is currently the owner of the right to divorce (i.e., he is the husband at the time of utterance), or (2) he attributes the divorce to future ownership, such as saying 'If I marry you, you are divorced' (attribution to the cause of ownership). The reasoning is that the consequence (al-jaza') must be likely to occur to instill fear, which fulfills the purpose of an oath (yamin) which is strength (quwwah) and manifestation (zuhur). Attributing to the cause of ownership (sabab al-milk) is equivalent to attributing to ownership because the consequence becomes apparent when the cause occurs. The commentary then gives a practical application: if a man says to a non-marriageable woman (ajnabiyyah) 'If you enter the house, you are divorced,' then later marries her, and she enters the house, no divorce occurs. This is because at the time of the statement, he was not the owner (she was not his wife), nor did he attribute the divorce to ownership or its cause (he did not say 'if I marry you, you are divorced'). The rule is derived from the principle that for a suspended divorce to be valid, the speaker must have some connection to the right to divorce at the time of utterance—either actual ownership or a clear link to future ownership.

Key Terms
حالف (halif): The person swearing the oath; in this context, the husband or person making a conditional statement of divorce.
جزاء (jaza'): The consequence that is attached to the condition; in ta'liq, it is the divorce itself that occurs upon condition.
سبب الملک (sabab al-milk): The cause of ownership; e.g., marriage contract, purchase, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Yes, because marriage gives him ownership.
B) No, because at the time of the statement he was not the owner and did not attribute to ownership.
C) Yes, because the condition was set before marriage.
D) No, because the woman must be marriageable at the time of the statement.

Key Takeaway
For a suspended divorce to be valid, the speaker must either be the husband at the time of utterance or explicitly link the divorce to future ownership.

Words of Condition in Suspended Divorce
Lists and explains condition words

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the seven condition words used in suspended divorce and identify which is the purest conditional particle.

Core Idea
The word 'in' (ان) is the purest conditional particle, free from temporal meaning.

In Hanafi law, suspended divorce (ta'liq al-talaq) requires precise wording. This passage from Ashraf al-Hadaya introduces the seven Arabic words that can function as conditionals. Understanding each word's nuance helps ensure valid divorce oaths.

Guided Path
1
Memorize the seven condition words
List the seven words from the text: in (ان), idha (اذا), idhama (اذاما), kull (كل), kullama (كلما), mata (متی), matama (متی ما).
These are the only words used for ta'liq in Hanafi fiqh.
2
Understand the derivation of 'shart'
The term 'shart' (condition) is derived from 'alamah (sign). These words are signs that a violation (hanth) has occurred when the condition is fulfilled.
The word 'hanth' is used for oath violation.
3
Distinguish the pure condition (in)
The word 'in' (ان) is purely for condition because it lacks any temporal meaning. All other words are annexed (mulhaq) to it in function.
This is a key Hanafi distinction; other schools may treat other particles similarly.
4
Analyze the special case of 'kull'
The word 'kull' (كل) is not a true condition because it is followed by a noun, whereas conditions normally relate to verbs. However, it is included because a verb is attached to the noun that follows it, e.g., 'Every slave I buy is free.'
This annexation (ilhaq) expands the scope of condition words.

الفاظ شرط

Words of condition. And the words of condition are: 'in', 'idha', 'idhama', 'kull', 'kullama', 'mata', 'matama'. Because 'shart' (condition) is derived from 'alamah' (sign), and these words are such that verbs follow them, so they become signs of violation. Then the word 'in' is purely for condition because it has no meaning of time, and what is beyond it is annexed to it. And the word 'kull' is not really a condition because what follows it is a noun, whereas condition is that to which the consequence is attached, and consequences are attached to verbs. However, it has been annexed to condition due to the attachment of a verb to the noun that follows it, such as your saying 'Every slave I buy, he is free.' Translation: And the words of condition are 'in', 'idha', 'idhama', 'kull', 'kullama', 'mata', and 'matama'. Because 'shart' is derived from 'alamah' (sign). And these words are such that verbs are attached to them, so they become signs of violation. Then know that the word 'in' is purely for condition because it has no meaning of time, and words other than 'in' are annexed to it. And the word 'kull' is not really a condition because what follows it is a noun, while the condition is that to which the consequence is attached, and consequences are attached to verbs. However, it has been annexed to condition due to the attachment of a verb to the noun that follows it, like your statement 'Every slave I buy, he is free.'
Source pages p. 333

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hadaya lists the Arabic words that can be used to express a condition (shart) in suspended divorce (ta'liq al-talaq). The words are: 'in' (ان), 'idha' (اذا), 'idhama' (اذاما), 'kull' (كل), 'kullama' (كلما), 'mata' (متی), and 'matama' (متی ما). The term 'shart' is derived from 'alamah' (sign), and these words are signs that indicate that a violation (hanth) will occur if the condition is fulfilled. The word 'in' is the purest conditional particle because it does not carry any temporal meaning; other words are treated similarly by annexation. The word 'kull' (every) is not a true condition because it is followed by a noun (e.g., 'every slave'), whereas conditions normally relate to verbs (actions). However, it is included here because a verb is attached to the noun that follows it (e.g., 'I buy'), as in 'Every slave I buy is free.' This serves as a practical guide for drafting valid conditional divorce statements. The passage is incomplete in the scanned text, but the main point is the classification of condition words.

Key Terms
شرط (shart): Condition; a future event upon which the legal consequence (divorce) is made contingent.
ان (in): A conditional particle indicating a pure condition without temporal meaning; the most common word for ta'liq.
حنث (hanth): Violation of an oath; occurs when the condition is fulfilled, triggering the consequence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The word 'in' (ان) is the only pure conditional particle; other words are annexed to it, with 'kull' being a special case.

The Nature and Derivation of Condition Words in Hanafi Talaq
Explains condition word terminology and derivation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the term 'shart' in Hanafi talaq, explain why the author uses 'alfaz al-shart' instead of 'huruf al-shart', and identify 'in' as the original condition particle.

Core Idea
The condition word 'in' is the prototypical particle; 'shart' derives from 'alamah' through meaning-based derivation (ishtiqaq kabir).

In the Hanafi school of talaq, the precise understanding of condition words is crucial for determining when a suspended divorce takes effect. This passage from the commentary on Hidayah clarifies the terminology: why the author uses 'alfaz al-shart' (words of condition) rather than 'huruf al-shart' (particles of condition), and how the word 'shart' itself is derived from the concept of a sign (alamah).

Guided Path
1
Distinguish 'alfaz' from 'huruf'
Note that the author uses 'alfaz al-shart' (words of condition) instead of 'huruf al-shart' (particles of condition) because many condition words are nouns, not particles. This inclusive term covers both nouns and particles.
Key point: 'alfaz' is broader than 'huruf'.
2
Identify 'in' as the original condition particle
The word 'in' (if) is the original particle in the chapter of conditions because it has no additional temporal meaning; all other condition words are attached to 'in' and include its meaning.
Other particles like 'kullama' contain temporal meaning, making them secondary.
3
Analyze the derivation of 'shart'
The author explains that 'shart' is derived from 'alamah' (sign) through ishtiqaq kabir (great derivation), where two words share a proportion in meaning even if their letters differ. The commentator resolves an apparent contradiction by positing that 'shart' (with sukun on ra) is derived from a different word 'shart' (with fatha on shin and ra) meaning 'sign'.
Ishtiqaq kabir is distinct from ishtiqaq saghir (which requires letter correspondence).
4
Understand the role of 'kull'
The word 'kull' (every) is not itself a condition word because what follows it is a noun, not an action. But 'kull' is attached to a noun that is connected to an action (e.g., 'every slave I purchase' – the action 'purchase' is connected to 'slave'), so the construction functions as a condition.
Thus, 'kull' is treated as a condition in effect, though not in form.

کل سے جو متصل آتا ہے وہ اسم ہے۔ اور شرط وہ ہے جس کے ساتھ جزاء متعلق ہو۔ اور جزا ئیں افعال کے ساتھ متعلق ہوتی ہیں مگر یہ کہ کلمہ کل شرط کے ساتھ لاحق کر دیا گیا فعل کے متعلق ہونے کی وجہ سے اس اسم کے ساتھ جو کلمہ کل کے ساتھ متصل ہے۔ جیسے تیرا قول ہر غلام کہ میں اس کو خریدوں وہ آزاد ہے۔ تشریح مصنف نے کلمات شرط کو ان الفاظ شرط کے ساتھ تعبیر فرمایا نہ کہ حروف شرط کے ساتھ ۔ کیونکہ ان کلمات میں بیشتر اسماء میں ہیں نہ کہ حروف ۔ اسلئے الفاظ کے ساتھ تعبیر کیا گیا تا کہ اساء وحروف دونوں کو شامل ہو جائے ۔ اور کلمہ ان باب شرط میں اصل ہے اور باقی سب اس کی فرع ہیں۔
صاحب ہدایہ نے الفاظ شرط کی وجہ تسمیہ بیان کی ہے۔ حاصل یہ کہ شرط مشتق ہے اس شرط سے جس کے معنی علامت کے ہیں۔ باری تعالیٰ کا ارشاد ہے فقد جاء اشراطها ای علاماتها کہا جاتا ہے اشراط الساعة ای علامات الساعة ۔ اور یہ الفاظ ایسے ہیں جو افعال کے متصل ہوتے ہیں کلمہ کل کے علاوہ ۔ لہذا یہ حانث ہونے کی علامات ہوں گے۔ صاحب ہدایہ کی عبارت میں بظاہر ستقم ہے۔ کیونکہ صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ شرط مشتق ہے علامت سے۔ بظاہر یہ غلط ہے۔ کیونکہ اشتقاق سے مراداشتقاق کمبیر ہے۔اور اشتقاق کبیر کہتے ہیں دولفظوں کے درمیان لفظ اور معنی میں تناسب ۔ اور شرط اور علامت کے درمیان لفظی تناسب موجود نہیں۔ لہذا یہ کہنا کہ شرط مشتق ہے علامت سے کیسے درست ہوگا۔ اس وجہ سے خادم نے عبارت مقدر مان کر کہا کہ شرط بسكون الراء مشتق ہے شرط افتح الشين والراء سے جس کے معنی علامت کے ہیں۔ اس تقدیر پر ہدایہ کی عبارت بے غبار ہو جائے گی۔
.
فرماتے ہیں کہ کلمہ ان محض شرط کیلئے ہے۔ اور باب شرط میں یہی اصل اصل ہے۔ کیونکہ کلمہ ان میں وقت وغیرہ کے معنی نہیں پاۓ جائے۔ اور کلمہ ان کے علاوہ تمام کلمات کلمہ ان کے ساتھ لاحق ہیں، کلمہ ان کے معنی کو متضمن ہونے کی وجہ سے۔ اور کلمہ کل در حقیقت شرط نہیں۔ کیونکہ کلمہ کل سے جو متصل آتا ہے وہ اسم ہے۔ اور شرط وہ ہے جسکے ساتھ جزاء متعلق ہو۔ اور جزا فعل کے ساتھ متعلق ہوتی ہے نہ کہ اسم کے ساتھ مگر کلمہ کل کو شرط کے ساتھ لاحق کر دیا گیا کیونکہ فعل اس اسم کے ساتھ متصل ہے جو اسم کلمہ کل سے ملا ہوا ہے یعنی فعل اس اسم کیلئے لازم ہے جو اسم کلمہ کل سے متصل ہے مثلاً تیر اقول كل عبد اشتريته فهو حر ہے۔
جب شرط پائی جائے تو یمین منخل ہو کر ختم ہو جاتی ہے
He (the author of Hidayah) says: That which comes connected with 'kull' is a noun. And the condition is that with which the consequence is connected. And consequences are connected with actions, except that the word 'kull' is attached to the condition due to its connection with the action, with that noun which is connected with the word 'kull'. Like your saying: 'Every slave that I purchase is free.' Clarification: The author expressed the words of condition with these 'alfaz al-shart' and not with 'huruf al-shart', because most of these words are nouns, not particles. Therefore, he expressed with 'alfaz' (words) so that both nouns and particles are included. And the word 'in' is the original in the chapter of conditions, and all others are its branches. The author of Hidayah explained the reason for naming the words of condition. The summary is that 'shart' is derived from that 'shart' which means 'alamah (sign). Allah Almighty said: 'Faqad jaa'a ashraatuha' i.e., its signs. It is said 'ashratu al-saa'ah' i.e., signs of the hour. And these words are those that are connected with actions except the word 'kull'. Therefore, they will be signs of becoming sinful (hanith). In the text of the author of Hidayah, it appears to be 'staqam' [؟]. Because the author of Hidayah said that 'shart' is derived from 'alamah'. Apparently, this is wrong. Because by derivation (ishtiqaq) is meant ishtiqaq kabir (great derivation). And ishtiqaq kabir means that there is a proportion in wording and meaning between two words. And between 'shart' and 'alamah' there is no verbal proportion. Therefore, how can it be correct to say that 'shart' is derived from 'alamah'? For this reason, al-Khadim assumed a conjectural phrase and said that 'shart' (with sukun on ra) is derived from 'shart' (with fatha on shin and ra) which means sign. With this assumption, the text of Hidayah becomes unblemished. He (the commentator) says that the word 'in' is solely for condition. And in the chapter of conditions, it is the original. Because in the word 'in', meanings like time etc. are not found. And all words other than 'in' are attached to 'in', because they include the meaning of 'in'. And the word 'kull' is not actually a condition. Because what comes connected with 'kull' is a noun. And the condition is that with which the consequence is connected. And the consequence is connected with the action, not with the noun. But the word 'kull' has been attached to the condition because the action is connected with that noun which is joined with the word 'kull', i.e., the action is necessary for that noun which is connected with the word 'kull'. For example, your saying: 'Every slave I purchase is free.' When the condition is found, the oath is dissolved and ended.
Source pages p. 334

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Hidayah defines the nature of condition words in divorce law. The author explains that the term 'alfaz al-shart' is used broadly to include both nouns and particles, unlike 'huruf al-shart' which would only cover particles. The word 'in' (if) is the prototypical condition particle because it has no additional temporal meaning. The word 'kull' (every) is not a condition word itself but is attached to a noun that is connected to an action, so it functions as a condition. The derivation of 'shart' from 'alamah' (sign) is discussed; the commentator resolves an apparent difficulty by positing that 'shart' is derived from the word 'shart' with a different vowel pattern meaning sign, preserving the relationship. The concluding statement establishes that upon fulfillment of the condition, the oath is dissolved.

Key Terms
کلمہ ان (kalimat 'in): The word 'if' is the original particle for conditions in the chapter of conditions.
شرط (shart): Condition; here meaning a sign (alamah) and also the linguistic term for the condition clause.
جزاء (jaza'): The consequence of the condition, usually an action or legal effect.
اشتقاق (ishtiqaq): Derivation of one word from another; here ishtiqaq kabir based on meaning proportion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) kull
B) in
C) kullama
D) man

Key Takeaway
The exact classification of condition words is fundamental to determining when a suspended talaq takes effect.

Dissolution of Oath upon Fulfillment of Condition: The Exception of 'Kullama'
States the ruling that oath ends when condition occurs except with 'kullama'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when a conditional oath is dissolved and explain why 'kullama' is an exception, citing the Quranic proof.

Core Idea
A conditional oath ends when the condition occurs once, except for 'kullama' which requires repetition.

This passage from Al-Hidayah clarifies a crucial distinction in Hanafi jurisprudence regarding conditional oaths, particularly in divorce. While most condition words (like 'if', 'when') trigger the oath only once upon fulfillment, the word 'kullama' (whenever) demands repeated application. Understanding this exception is vital for correctly applying conditional divorces and avoiding unintended multiple divorces.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling
State that for most condition words (e.g., 'in', 'idha'), the oath is dissolved when the condition occurs once.
The condition must be fulfilled exactly once; after that, the oath is fully discharged.
2
Recognize the exception
Note that 'kullama' is the only word that does not dissolve the oath; instead, the oath remains active for each future occurrence of the condition.
The text explicitly excludes 'kullama' from the general rule.
3
Understand the linguistic basis
The passage explains that 'kullama' necessitates generality (umum) and repetition (tikrar) in language, whereas other condition words do not.
Linguistic analysis determines the legal effect.
4
Examine the Quranic proof
Allah's words 'Whenever their skins are burned' (Quran 4:56) use 'kullama' to indicate repeated action, establishing the principle of repetition.
The verse is cited as a linguistic precedent.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Consider a husband saying 'If you enter the house, you are divorced' vs. 'Whenever (kullama) you enter the house, you are divorced'. In the first, one entry triggers one divorce and the oath ends; in the second, each entry triggers a new divorce and the oath continues.
This distinction is critical in marital law.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ففى هذه الالفاظ اذا وجد الشرط انحلت وانتهت اليمين لانها غير مقتضية للعموم والتكرار لغة فبوجود الفعل مرة يتم الشرط ولابقاء لليمين بدونه الافى كلمة كلما فانها تقتضى تعميم الافعال قال الله تعالى كلما نضجت جلودهم الآية و من ضرورة التعيم التكرار

ترجمہ قدوری نے کہا۔ پس ان الفاظ میں جب شرط پائی گئی تو قسم محل ہو کر ختم ہو گئی ۔ کیونکہ یہ الفاظ لغت میں عموم و تکرار کو تقاضا نہیں ۔ پس ایک مرتبہ فعل کے پائے جانے کی وجہ سے شرط پوری ہو جائے گی اور بغیر شرط کے یمین باقی نہیں رہتی مگر کلمہ کلما میں اس لئے کہ وہ افعال کی تقسیم کا تقاضا کرتا ہے اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا۔ جب ان کی کھالیں جل جائیں گی (الآیۃ ) اور تمیم کے لوازم میں سے تکرار ہے۔

تشریح کلمہ کلما کے علاوہ تمام الفاظ شرط کا حکم یہ ہے کہ جب شرط پائی گئی تو یمین منحل ہو کر ختم ہو جائے گی ۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ کلمہ کلما کے علاوہ باقی الفاظ شرط لغتہ عموم و تکرار کا تقاضا نہیں کرتے ہیں۔ لہذا ایک مرتبہ فعل کے پائے جانے سے شرط پوری ہو جائے گی ۔ اور بغیر شرط یمین باقی نہیں رہتی۔ اور رہا کلمہ کلما چونکہ وہ افعال میں تعمیم کا تقاضا کرتا ہے جیسے باری تعالی کا قول كلما نضجت جلودهم الآیۃ۔ اور تعمیم کیلئے تکرار لازم ہے۔ اسلئے کلمہ کلما میں شرط کے پائے جانے کے بعد بھی یمین باقی رہے گی۔
He (Quduri) said: So in these words, when the condition is found, the oath is dissolved and ended, because these words do not necessitate generality and repetition linguistically. So with the occurrence of the action once, the condition is completed, and the oath has no continuation without it, except in the word 'kullama', because it necessitates the generalization of actions. Allah Almighty said: 'Whenever their skins are burned...' (the verse). And from the necessity of generalization is repetition.

Translation (of Quduri): Quduri said: So in these words, when the condition is found, the oath is dissolved and ended. Because these words do not necessitate generality and repetition in language. So with the occurrence of the action once, the condition is fulfilled, and the oath does not remain without the condition, except in the word 'kullama', because it necessitates the distribution of actions. Allah Almighty said: 'When their skins are burned...' (the verse). And from the necessities of generalization is repetition.

Clarification: The ruling of all words of condition except 'kullama' is that when the condition is found, the oath is dissolved and ended. The proof is that the other words of condition do not necessitate generality and repetition linguistically. Therefore, with one occurrence of the action, the condition is fulfilled, and the oath does not remain without the condition. As for the word 'kullama', since it necessitates generalization in actions, like the saying of Allah Almighty: 'Whenever their skins are burned...' (the verse). And generalization necessitates repetition. Therefore, in 'kullama', even after the condition is found, the oath will remain.
Source pages p. 334

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Quduri's text in Hidayah establishes a key principle in conditional divorce: except for the word 'kullama' (whenever), all condition words (such as 'in', 'idha') when used in oaths of divorce do not imply repetition. Once the condition occurs one time, the oath is fully discharged and cannot cause further divorces. The exception is 'kullama', which linguistically requires generalization and repetition, as evidenced by the Quranic verse 4:56 'Whenever their skins are burned, We replace them with other skins.' Thus, with 'kullama', the oath continues to apply for each instance the condition occurs.

Key Terms
کلمہ کلما (kalimat kullama): The word 'whenever' which implies generalization and repetition of the condition.
عموم (umum): Generality of actions; the property of applying to all instances.
تکرار (tikrar): Repetition; a necessary consequence of generalization.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which word of condition requires repetition of the condition for the oath to continue?
A) in
B) idha
C) kullama
D) kull

Key Takeaway
The word 'kullama' in conditional oaths implies repetition, so the oath continues for each occurrence of the condition.

Exhaustion of Consequence in Conditional Divorce ('Kullama')
Branch ruling on 'kullama' after triple divorce and halala

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that a conditional oath ends when its consequence is exhausted, and apply it to the case of 'kullama' after triple divorce and halala.

Core Idea
When the owned divorces are used up, the oath vanishes.

This lesson examines a specific branch of conditional divorce using the word 'kullama' (whenever). If a husband says 'Whenever you enter the house, you are divorced', each entry triggers a divorce. After three entries, the marriage ends. After a halala, the couple may remarry, but what happens if the wife enters the house again? The Hanafi school rules that no divorce occurs because the husband no longer owns any divorces from that marriage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition and its format
The husband used 'kullama', which makes each occurrence of the condition a separate trigger. Note that this is different from 'in' (if) which only triggers once.
With 'kullama', each entry is a new event.
2
Count the number of triggered divorces
If the wife enters three times, three divorces occur, exhausting the husband's right to divorce in that marriage. The marriage becomes irrevocably terminated (ba'in).
After triple divorce, the husband cannot remarry her without halala.
3
Understand the halala and remarriage
After another husband (muhallil) marries and divorces her, the first husband may remarry her. Now the condition is still phrased as 'kullama', but the owned divorces are reset?
Actually, the ownership of divorces is per marriage; after remarriage, the husband again owns three divorces? The text says no – the original oath's consequence is exhausted.
4
Analyze the Hanafi reasoning
The oath consists of the condition and the consequence. The consequence was the three divorces owned in that original marriage. Once those divorces are spent, the consequence no longer exists. An oath cannot remain without its consequence.
Therefore, the oath itself has ended.
5
Apply to the remarriage scenario
In the new marriage, the condition 'kullama' is not renewed; the original oath is dead. Thus, entering the house does not trigger any divorce.
Imam Zafar disagreed, but the majority holds that no divorce occurs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كلما دخلت الدار فانت طالق پر متفرع مسئله
قال فان تروجها بعد ذلک اى بعد زوج اخر وتكرر الشرط لم يقع شيء لان باستيفاء الطلقات الثلث المملوكات في هذا النكاح لم يبق الجزاء وبقاء اليمين به وبالشرط وفيه خلاف زفر وسنقرره من بعد ان شاء الله تعالى

ترجمہ قدوری نے کہا پس اگر اس کے بعد اس عورت سے نکاح کیا یعنی زوج آخر سے حلالہ کے بعد اور شرط مکرر پائی گئی تو کوئی چیز واقع نہیں ہوگی۔ کیونکہ اس نکاح میں اپنی مملوکہ تین طلاقوں کو وصول کر لینے کی وجہ سے۔ جزاء باقی نہیں رہی۔ اور قسم کی بقاء جزاء اور شرط کے ساتھ ہے۔ اور اس میں اختلاف ہے امام زفر کا ۔ اور ہم اس کو ان شاء اللہ بعد میں ثابت کریں گے۔

تشریح یہ مسئلہ کلما پر متفرع ہے۔ چنانچہ اگر کسی نے اپنی بیوی سے کہا كلما دخلت الدار فانت طالق ۔ پس عورت یکے بعد دیگرے تین مرتبہ گھر میں داخل ہوئی تو اس کو تین طلاقیں واقع ہو جائیں گی۔ پس زوج ثانی سے حلالہ کے بعد یہ عورت زوج اول کے نکاح میں آگئی اور شرط مکرر پائی گئی۔ یعنی وہ عورت پھر گھر میں داخل ہو گئی تو اب کوئی طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی ۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ شوہر سابقہ نکاح کی وجہ سے جن تین طلاقوں کا مالک تھاوہ پوری ہو گئیں ۔ لہذا جزاء باقی نہ رہی۔ کیونکہ جزاء اس ملک کی تین طلاقیں تھیں ۔ پس جب جزا منتفی ہو گئی تو قسم بھی ختم ہوگئی ۔ کیونکہ قسم شرط و جزاء کے ذکر کا نام ہے اور جب قسم ختم ہوگئی تو دخول دار کے بعد طلاق واقع ہونے کے کیا معنی ہیں۔ اسلئے ہم نے کہا کہ اس صورت میں طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی۔
Branch issue on 'kullama dakhalti al-dar fa-anti taliq'
He (Quduri) said: If he marries her after that, i.e., after another husband, and the condition repeats, nothing occurs because by exhausting the three owned divorces in this marriage, the consequence (jaza') does not remain, and the oath remains with it and the condition. And there is a difference of opinion of Zafar, and we will establish it later, God willing.

Translation: Quduri said: So after that, if he marries this woman, i.e., after a second husband (halala), and the condition repeats, nothing will occur. Because in this marriage, by exhausting the three owned divorces, the consequence did not remain. And the continuation of the oath is with the consequence and the condition. And there is a difference of Imam Zafar, and we will establish it later, God willing.

Clarification: This issue is a branch on 'kullama'. So if a man said to his wife: 'Whenever you enter the house, you are divorced.' Then the woman entered the house three times consecutively, three divorces occur. Then after halala with a second husband, this woman came into the marriage of the first husband, and the condition repeated, i.e., the woman again entered the house; then now no divorce will occur. The proof is that the husband, due to the previous marriage, owned three divorces, and those were completed. Therefore, the consequence did not remain. Because the consequence was the three divorces of this ownership. So when the consequence is negated, the oath also ends. Because the oath is the name for the mention of condition and consequence. And when the oath is gone, what meaning is there for divorce to occur after entering the house? Therefore, we said that in this case, no divorce will occur.
Source pages p. 335

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific application of the word 'kullama' in divorce. If a husband says to his wife 'Whenever you enter the house, you are divorced' using 'kullama', each entry triggers a divorce. If she enters three times, three divorces occur, ending the marriage. After a halala (intervening marriage and divorce), she remarries the first husband. If she then enters the house again, no divorce occurs. The reasoning is that in the original marriage, the husband owned three divorces, and all have been used up. The consequence (jaza') of the oath was those three divorces. Since the consequence is exhausted, the oath itself ends. The Hanafi position is that the oath consists of both condition and consequence; without the consequence, the oath cannot persist. Imam Zafar differed, claiming the oath continues, but the relied-upon view is that it does not.

Key Terms
جزاء (jaza'): The consequence of the condition; here specifically the three divorces that the husband owns.
حلالہ (halala): An intervening marriage that allows remarriage after triple divorce.
مملوکہ طلاق (mamluk talaq): The divorces owned by the husband in the current marriage (up to three).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of 'kullama dakhalti al-dar fa-anti taliq', after three divorces and halala, what happens if the wife enters the house again?
A) One divorce occurs
B) One more divorce occurs
C) No divorce occurs
D) The marriage becomes forbidden

Key Takeaway
A conditional oath with 'kullama' ends when its consequence is exhausted; after triple divorce and halala, no further divorce occurs upon re-entry.

6 min
Divorce Conditioned on Future Marriage with 'Kullama'
Rules that each marriage after the oath causes divorce even after halala

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a husband says 'Whenever I marry a woman, she is divorced' and explain why it applies to each subsequent marriage including after halala.

Core Idea
Every new marriage triggers the divorce condition because the husband's ownership of divorce via marriage is unlimited.

This lesson examines a specific conditional divorce formula. When a husband uses 'kullama' (whenever) tied to the act of marriage itself, the divorce occurs with every new marriage he contracts, regardless of any intervening halala. Understanding the legal rationale—based on unlimited marital capacity—is essential for correct application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key phrase and its scope
Look at the condition: 'kullama tazawwajtu imra'atan fahiya taliq'. Note that 'kullama' indicates repetition and 'imra'atan' is indefinite, referring to any woman he marries.
This is distinct from a condition tied to a specific woman.
2
Distinguish from conditional on a specific wife
If he says 'If I marry Zaynab, she is divorced,' the oath is limited to that one marriage. Here, the indefinite 'imra'atan' makes the oath recurrent.
The difference lies in the generality of the object.
3
Understand the legal basis (illah)
The oath is based on the husband's ownership of divorce through marriage. In each new marriage, he acquires the right to divorce that wife. Since marriage is unlimited (ghayr mahsur), the oath applies to each marriage.
The husband never loses the capacity to own divorce via a new marriage.
4
Apply the ruling after halala
Even if he marries, divorces, performs halala with another man, and then remarries the same woman, the condition triggers again because it is a new marriage.
Halala does not nullify the original oath; the oath is attached to the act of marriage itself.

Source Text
