ولود خلت على نفس التزوج بان قال كلما تزوجت امرأة فهي طالق يحنث بكل مرة و ان كان بعد زوج اخر لان انعقادها باعتبار مایملک عليها من الطلاق بالتزوج وذلك غير محصور

ترجمہ اور اگر ( کلمہ کلما) نفس تزوج پر داخل ہوا بایں طور کہ کہا کہ جب میں کسی عورت سے نکاح کروں تو وہ طالقہ ہے۔ ہر مرتبہ سے حانث ہو جائے گا۔ اگر چہ زوج آخر کے بعد کیونکہ یمین کا منعقد ہونا اس اعتبار سے ہے کہ وہ تزوج کی وجہ سے طلاق کا مالک ہے۔ اور تزوج غیر محدود ہے۔

تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے نفس تزوج پر کلمہ کلمہ داخل کر کے یہ کہا كلما تزوجت امرأة فهي طالق تو شخص ہر مرتبہ نکاح سے حانث ہو جائے گا۔ اگر چہ زوج ثانی کے ساتھ حلالہ کرنے کے بعد ہی کیوں نہ کیا ہو۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ یمین اسلئے منعقد ہوتی ہے
And if it (kullama) is made to enter upon the act of marriage itself, such that he says: 'Whenever I marry a woman, she is divorced,' he becomes sinful (hanith) with every time, even if it is after another husband, because its contraction is based on what he owns of divorce through marriage, and that is unlimited.

Translation: And if (the word kullama) is made to enter upon the act of marriage itself, in that he says: 'Whenever I marry a woman, she is divorced,' he will be a sinner with every marriage, even if it is after a second husband, because the contraction of the oath is based on the fact that he owns divorce due to marriage, and marriage is unlimited.

Clarification: The issue is that if someone made 'kullama' enter upon the act of marriage itself by saying 'Whenever I marry a woman, she is divorced,' the person will be a sinner with every marriage, even if it is after doing halala with a second husband. The proof is that the oath is contracted because...
Source pages p. 335

Commentary
This passage distinguishes between two uses of 'kullama'. When the condition is linked to the husband's own act of marriage (e.g., 'Whenever I marry a woman, she is divorced'), the oath applies to each new marriage he contracts, including after a halala. The reason is that in each new marriage, the husband owns three divorces, so the consequence (divorce) is always possible. Since the husband's capacity to marry is not limited, the oath continues. The term 'hanith' means he falls into sin by violating the oath, but here it means the divorce takes effect. The text notes that this ruling holds even if the marriage is after a halala with a second husband.

Key Terms
نفس التزوج (nafs al-tazawwuj): The act of marrying itself, as opposed to a specific woman.
حانث (hanith): One who breaks an oath; here meaning the divorce occurs and he incurs sin.
انعقاد (in'iqad): Contraction of the oath; the oath is formed and becomes binding.
غیر محصور (ghayr mahsur): Unlimited, not confined; the number of marriages a man can contract is not limited.

General Ruling on Conditional Words (Except 'Kullama')
Explanation of the general rule for conditional words except 'kullama'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for conditional oaths using words that do not imply repetition, and apply it to a given scenario.

Core Idea
For words other than 'kullama', the oath dissolves upon the first fulfillment of the condition.

In Hanafi fiqh, the effect of a conditional oath depends on the specific word used. Most conditional words—like 'in' (if) or 'idha' (when)—do not inherently imply repetition. Therefore, when the condition occurs once, the oath is fulfilled and terminates. This lesson explains the general principle and its linguistic reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditional word
Look at the word used to introduce the condition. Common words include 'in' (if), 'idha' (when), and 'kullama' (every time). Determine which one is used.
For this lesson, we focus on words other than 'kullama'.
2
Assess linguistic property
Determine if the word lexically demands generality and repetition (ta'mim and takrar). Most words do not; only 'kullama' does.
General rule: words other than 'kullama' do not imply repetition.
3
Apply the rule to the scenario
If the word does not imply repetition, then upon the first occurrence of the condition, the oath (yamin) is fulfilled and dissolves. No further legal effect remains.
The condition is satisfied once and the oath ends.
4
Conclude
The oath terminates, and any subsequent occurrence of the same action has no effect on the original oath.
This is the general Hanafi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تشریح کلمہ کلما کے علاوہ تمام الفاظ شرط کا حکم یہ ہے کہ جب شرط پائی گئی تو یمین منحل ہو کر ختم ہو جائے گی ۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ کلمہ کلما کے علاوہ باقی الفاظ شرط لغتہ عموم و تکرار کا تقاضا نہیں کرتے ہیں۔ لہذا ایک مرتبہ فعل کے پائے جانے سے شرط پوری ہو جائے گی ۔ اور بغیر شرط یمین باقی نہیں رہتی۔ اور رہا کلمہ کلمتو چونکہ وہ افعال میں تعمیم کا تقاضا کرتا ہے جیسے باری تعالی کا قول كلما نضجت جلودهم الآیۃ۔ اور تمیم کیلئے تکرار لازم ہے۔ اسلئے کلمہ کلما میں شرط کے پائے جانے کے بعد بھی یمین باقی رہے گی۔
Explanation: The ruling for all conditional words other than 'kullama' is that when the condition is found, the oath dissolves and terminates. The proof is that conditional words other than 'kullama' lexically do not demand generality and repetition. Therefore, with a single occurrence of the action, the condition is fulfilled. Without the condition, the oath does not remain. As for the word 'kullama', since it demands generalization in actions, like Allah's saying 'Every time their skins are roasted...' (Quran 4:56). And for generalization, repetition is necessary. Therefore, with the word 'kullama', even after the condition is found, the oath remains.
Source pages p. 335

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi perspective. It establishes a fundamental distinction in conditional oaths (yamin) between the word 'kullama' (every time) and other conditional words. For all other words (such as 'in' or 'idha'), the oath is fulfilled and ends when the condition occurs once. The reasoning is linguistic: these words do not inherently imply repetition. For 'kullama', however, it is different. The word itself demands generality and repetition, as evidenced by its usage in the Quran (4:56: 'Every time their skins are roasted, We replace them with other skins'). Because 'kullama' necessitates repetition (takrar), the oath remains in effect even after the first occurrence of the condition; it continues to be binding for subsequent occurrences. This is a key principle in Hanafi fiqh for conditional divorces and oaths.

Key Terms
یمین (yamin): An oath or solemn declaration, often used in the context of conditional divorce.
ان (in): A common conditional word meaning 'if'. It does not imply repetition.
اذ (idha): A conditional word meaning 'when' or 'whenever'. It does not imply repetition in Hanafi usage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The oath dissolves and no further divorce occurs upon subsequent entries.
B) The oath remains and she is divorced every time she enters.
C) She must be divorced three times.
D) The divorce is invalid because the word 'in' is insufficient.

Key Takeaway
For conditional words other than 'kullama', the oath dissolves upon the first occurrence of the condition; it does not remain active for subsequent occurrences.

The Unique Nature of 'Kullama' in Conditional Oaths
Explanation of the unique case of 'kullama' and its Quranic proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why 'kullama' ('every time') is treated differently from other conditional words, cite the Quranic proof, and apply the rule to examples.

Core Idea
The word 'kullama' implies repetition, so the oath remains for each occurrence of the condition.

Unlike other conditional words, the Arabic word 'kullama' (every time) inherently demands generality and repetition. This is demonstrated by its use in the Quran (4:56). Consequently, in Hanafi fiqh, an oath using 'kullama' does not dissolve upon the first fulfillment; rather, it continues to be binding for every subsequent occurrence. This lesson delves into the linguistic and textual evidence for this unique ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the exception
Recognize that 'kullama' is the only conditional word that does not follow the general rule. It demands generality (ta'mim) in actions.
The general rule applies to all other words.
2
Analyze the linguistic meaning
'Kullama' lexically implies that the condition applies to every instance of the action. This necessitates repetition (takrar).
Repetition is a necessary consequence of generality.
3
Examine the Quranic proof
Allah says: 'Every time (kullama) their skins are roasted, We replace them with other skins' (4:56). The repetition of the action is evident from the word 'kullama'.
The verse shows that the action occurs repeatedly, not just once.
4
Apply the rule
When a conditional oath uses 'kullama', the condition is fulfilled each time the action occurs. The oath does not dissolve; it remains active for future occurrences.
Each occurrence triggers the legal consequence (e.g., divorce).

Source Text

Without the condition, the oath does not remain. As for the word 'kullama', since it demands generalization in actions, like Allah's saying 'Every time their skins are roasted...' (Quran 4:56). And for generalization, repetition is necessary. Therefore, with the word 'kullama', even after the condition is found, the oath remains.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi perspective. It establishes a fundamental distinction in conditional oaths (yamin) between the word 'kullama' (every time) and other conditional words. For all other words (such as 'in' or 'idha'), the oath is fulfilled and ends when the condition occurs once. The reasoning is linguistic: these words do not inherently imply repetition. For 'kullama', however, it is different. The word itself demands generality and repetition, as evidenced by its usage in the Quran (4:56: 'Every time their skins are roasted, We replace them with other skins'). Because 'kullama' necessitates repetition (takrar), the oath remains in effect even after the first occurrence of the condition; it continues to be binding for subsequent occurrences. This is a key principle in Hanafi fiqh for conditional divorces and oaths.

Divorce Every Time You Marry: The Unlimited Condition
Ruling on kullama conditional divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on conditional divorce when the condition is the act of marriage itself, and explain the qiyas-based reasoning that repetition of the cause (marriage) necessitates repetition of the effect (divorce).

Core Idea
Every new marriage renews the divorce — because marriage is unlimited, its effect is unlimited.

In this lesson, we examine a specific type of conditional divorce where the condition is the act of marriage itself. Unlike conditions tied to a wife's specific actions (which may be limited), the act of marriage is inherently unlimited — a man can marry any number of women. The Hanafi masters derive the ruling using qiyas: repetition of the cause (marriage) necessitates repetition of the effect (divorce). This principle ensures that each new marriage triggers a fresh divorce, even after halala.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
The condition is the act of marriage itself (tazawwuj), not an act of the wife. The man says 'Every time I marry a woman, she is divorced.'
Contrast with cases where the condition is the wife entering a house, which is limited by the number of divorces already given.
2
Determine the legal basis
The oath is effective because upon marriage the husband owns the right to divorce. This ownership arises from the marriage contract itself.
Hanafi: talaq is a right of the husband that becomes operative upon marriage.
3
Apply the principle of cause and effect
Since marriage can be repeated without limit (a man can marry any woman, even the same woman after halala), the effect (divorce) must also be unlimited. The maxim 'repetition of cause necessitates repetition of effect' governs.
This is a qiyas jali (clear analogy) — the cause (marriage) is the illa for the husband's ownership of divorce.
4
Confirm the practical consequence
Every new marriage, including remarrying the same woman after halala, triggers the divorce immediately. The oath is never exhausted.
Even if the man marries a hundred women, each is divorced upon marriage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كلما تزوجت امراة فهي طالق سے معلق کرنے کا حکم
ولود خلت على نفس التزوج بان قال كلما تزوجت امرأة فهي طالق يحنث بكل مرة و ان كان بعد زوج اخر لان انعقادها باعتبار مایملک عليها من الطلاق بالتزوج وذلك غير محصور ترجمہ اور اگر ( کلمہ کلما) نفس تزوج پر داخل ہوا بایں طور کہ کہا کہ جب میں کسی عورت سے نکاح کروں تو وہ طالقہ ہے۔ ہر مرتبہ سے حانث ہو جائے گا۔ اگر چہ زوج آخر کے بعد کیونکہ یمین کا منعقد ہونا اس اعتبار سے ہے کہ وہ تزوج کی وجہ سے طلاق کا مالک ہے۔ اور تزوج غیر محدود ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے نفس تزوج پر کلمہ کلمۂ اخل کر کے یہ کہا كلما تزوجت امرأة فهي طالق تو شخص ہر مرتبہ نکاح سے حانث وہ جائے گا۔ اگر چہ زوج ثانی کے ساتھ حلالہ کرنے کے بعد ہی کیوں نہ کیا ہو۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ یمین اسلئے منعقد ہوتی ہے کہ یہ شخص نکاح کرنے کی وجہ سے طلاق کا مالک ہو جاتا ہے۔ اور نکاح کرنا غیر محدود ہے لہذا طلاق بھی غیر محدود ہو گی ۔ اسلئے کہ تکرار سبب تکرار مسبب کا تقاضا کرتا ہے۔
Ruling on suspending with 'kullama tazawwajtu imra'atan fahiya taliq'. And if it comes upon the act of marriage itself, such that he says 'Every time I marry a woman, she is divorced', he breaks the oath with every time, even if after another husband, because its effectiveness is by virtue of what he owns of divorce upon marriage, and that is unlimited. Translation: And if (the word 'kullama') enters upon the act of marriage itself, in the manner that he says 'When I marry a woman, she is divorced', he will break the oath every time, even if after another husband, because the oath's effectiveness is by virtue that he owns divorce due to marriage, and marriage is unlimited. Commentary: The issue is that if a person puts the word 'kullama' upon the act of marriage itself and says 'Every time I marry a woman, she is divorced', the person will break the oath every time he marries, even if after halala with a second husband. The proof is that the oath is effective because this person becomes the owner of divorce by virtue of marriage, and marriage is unlimited. Therefore, divorce is also unlimited, because repetition of the cause necessitates repetition of the effect.
Source pages p. 335

Commentary
This passage addresses a different scenario: a man says 'Every time I marry a woman, she is divorced' (kullama tazawwajtu imra'atan fahiya taliq). Here, the condition is the act of marriage itself, not an act of the wife. The ruling is that every time he marries a woman, that woman becomes divorced immediately. This applies even after halala; if he remarries the same woman after halala, she is divorced again. The reason is that the basis of the oath is the man's ownership of divorce upon marriage. Since marriage is not limited (he can marry an unlimited number of times, even the same woman after halala), the effect (divorce) is also unlimited. This is an application of the qiyas principle that repetition of the cause necessitates repetition of the effect. Unlike the previous case where the condition was the wife's entry into the house (which was limited to three in that marriage), here the condition is marriage itself, which is not limited. Thus, each new marriage triggers the divorce.

Key Terms
تزوج (tazawwuj): The act of marriage, which here is the condition for the oath.
حنث (hanath): To break an oath or to be in a state of violation of the oath. Here, it means the divorce occurs as a consequence of the oath.

Key Takeaway
When a conditional divorce is tied to the act of marriage itself, each new marriage (even after halala) results in an immediate, valid divorce, because marriage as a cause is unlimited.

Survival of Conditional Divorce Oath After Loss of Ownership
Principle of oath survival after loss of ownership of wife

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state and explain the Hanafi ruling that a conditional divorce oath (ta'liq al-talaq) is not invalidated by the husband's loss of ownership of his wife after swearing, and apply the rational proof distinguishing between the inception and survival of the oath.

Core Idea
A conditional divorce oath survives loss of ownership because inception does not require ownership, so survival requires it even less.

This lesson examines a key Hanafi principle in ta'liq al-talaq: if a husband suspends a divorce on a condition and then divorces his wife before the condition occurs, the conditional oath remains valid. The proof is rational (dalil aqli): an oath can be taken before marriage when no ownership exists, so by priority (awlawi), its survival after loss of ownership is even less demanding. We will explore the ruling, the proof, and two practical scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Legal Ruling
State the Hanafi position: a conditional divorce oath is not invalidated by the husband's loss of ownership of his wife after the oath.
The ruling is taken from al-Quduri's matn and is the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school.
2
Understand the Rational Proof (Dalil Aqli)
Analyze the a fortiori argument: the inception of an oath (e.g., 'If I marry you, you are divorced') does not require ownership, so survival after loss of ownership is even less demanding.
The proof compares inception (starting a new oath without ownership) with survival (continuing an existing oath without ownership).
3
Distinguish Between Two Scenarios
Apply the ruling: (1) If the condition occurs after remarriage (ownership regained), the divorce takes effect. (2) If the condition occurs before remarriage (no ownership), the oath is fulfilled but no divorce occurs because the subject (the wife) is no longer a valid object of divorce.
The key factor is whether the wife is under the husband's ownership at the moment the condition is fulfilled.
4
Address a Potential Objection
Consider the objection: if the consequence (divorce) requires ownership to occur, how can the oath survive without ownership? The Hanafi response: the oath's survival does not require ownership; only the occurrence of the consequence when the condition is met requires ownership.
This distinction between the oath's existence and its execution is crucial.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
یمین کے بعد ملک کا زوال اس کو باطل نہیں کرتا
قال وزوال الملك بعد اليمين لا يبطلها لانه لم يوجد الشرط فبقى والجزاء باق لبقاء محله فبقى اليمين ثم ان وجد الشرط فى ملكه انحلت اليمين ووقع الطلاق لانه وجد الشرط والمحل قابل للجزاء فينزل الجزاء ولا يبقى اليمين لماقلنا وان وجدفى غير الملک انحلت اليمين لوجود الشرط ولم يقع شئى لانعدام المحلية
ترجمہ قدوری نے کہا اور ملک کا زائل ہو نا ختم کے بعد قسم کو باطل نہیں کرتا۔ کیونکہ شرط نہیں پائی گئی تو قسم باقی رہی ۔ اور جزاء کا محل ( عورت ) باقی ہونے سے جزاء باقی ہے تو یمین بھی باقی ہے۔ پھر اگر مرد کی ملک میں شرط پائی گئی تو قسم اتری اور طلاق واقع ہو گئی۔ کیونکہ شرط پائی گئی اور محل قابل جزاء ہے۔ پس جزاء نازل ہوگی اور یمین باقی نہیں رہے گی اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے بیان کی ہے۔ اور اگر غیر ملک میں شرط پائی گئی تو یمین اتر گئی۔ شرط کے پائے جانے کی وجہ سے ۔ اور کوئی ( طلاق ) واقع نہ ہوگی محل کے معدوم ہونے کی وجہ سے۔
تشریح صاحب قدوری نے ایک اصول ذکر کیا ہے۔ وہ یہ کہ اگر قسم کے بعد مرد کی ملک زائل ہوگئی تو قسم باطل نہیں ہوگی ۔ صورت اس کی یہ ہے کہ مرد نے اپنی بیوی سے کہا ان دخلت الدار فانت طالق ۔ پھر دخول دار سے پہلے ہی اس عورت کو بائنہ کر دیا اس زوال ملک کی وجہ سے یمین باطل نہیں ہوگی۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ یمین کی بقاء شرط اور جزاء سے ہے اور مفروض یہ ہے کہ شرط نہیں پائی گئی ۔ لہذا شرط باقی ہے اور بقائمل کی وجہ سے جزاء بھی باقی ہے۔ پس جب شرط اور جزاء دونوں باقی ہیں تو سیمین بھی باقی ہے۔ لیکن اگر کوئی سوال کرے کہ یہ تسلیم ہے کہ محل جزاء باقی ہے مگر جزاء کے واقع ہونے کیلئے ملک شرط ہے اور یہاں ملک غیر موجود ہے۔ پس یمین باقی نہ رہنی چاہئے ۔ جواب۔ ہمارا کلام وقوع جزاء میں نہیں ہے۔ بلکہ بقاء یمین میں ہے۔ اور یمین ابتداء ملک کی محتاج نہیں۔ کیونکہ ان تزوجتک فانت طالق جائز ہے۔ حالانکہ اس وقت حالف طلاق کا مالک نہیں ہے پس جب ابتداء یمین محتاج ملک نہیں تو بقاء بدرجہ اولیٰ محتاج ملک نہیں ہوگی۔ کیونکہ ابتداء کے مقابلہ میں بقاء آسان ہے۔
پھر اس کے بعد دوصورتیں ہیں۔ یہ کہ شرط ملک میں پائی جائے مثلاً اس شخص نے اس عورت کے ساتھ دوبارہ نکاح کیا پھر شرط پائی گئی۔
(۲) یہ کہ شرط غیر ملک میں پائی گئی مثلاً دوبارہ نکاح سے پہلے ہی شرط پائی گئی۔ پس صورت اول میں طلاق واقع ہوگئی۔ اور یمین پوری ہو گئی۔ طلاق تو اسلئے واقع ہو گئی کہ شرط ( دخول دار ) ملک میں پائی گئی لہذا جزاء ( طلاق ) جو اس کے ساتھ متعلق ہے وہ بھی واقع ہوگئی ۔ اور یمین کا پورا ہونا اسلئے ہے کہ کلام میں جو لفظ ان ہے وہ تکرار پر دلالت نہیں کرتا ۔ لہذا ایک مرتبہ شرط پائے جانے کی وجہ سے یمین پوری ہوگئی اور صورت ثانیہ میں یمین تو پوری ہوگئی کیونکہ شرط پائی گئی ہے البتہ طلاق واقع نہیں ہوئی کیونکہ محل معدوم ہے۔
Loss of ownership after the oath does not invalidate it. He (al-Quduri) said: And loss of ownership after the oath does not invalidate it because the condition did not occur, so it remains, and the consequence remains due to the survival of its subject, so the oath remains. Then, if the condition occurs while in his ownership, the oath is fulfilled and divorce occurs because the condition occurred and the subject is capable of the consequence, so the consequence descends and the oath does not remain for what we stated. And if it occurs outside of ownership, the oath is fulfilled due to the occurrence of the condition, and nothing occurs due to the non-existence of the subject. Translation: al-Quduri said: And loss of ownership after the oath does not invalidate it because the condition did not occur, so the oath remained. And since the subject (the woman) of the consequence remains, the consequence remains, so the oath also remains. Then, if the condition occurs while in the husband's ownership, the oath is fulfilled and divorce occurs because the condition occurred and the subject is capable of consequence, so the consequence descends and the oath will not remain due to the reason we stated. And if the condition occurs outside of ownership, the oath is fulfilled due to the occurrence of the condition, and nothing (of divorce) occurs due to the non-existence of the subject. Commentary: The author al-Quduri mentioned a principle: if the husband's ownership of the wife ceases after the oath, the oath is not invalidated. Example: a man says to his wife, 'If you enter the house, you are divorced.' Then before she enters, he divorces her with a irrevocable divorce (bain). Due to this loss of ownership, the oath is not invalidated. The proof: the survival of the oath depends on the condition and the consequence; it is assumed that the condition did not occur, so the condition remains, and due to the survival of the subject (the wife), the consequence also remains. Thus, when both condition and consequence remain, the oath also remains. If one objects: we accept that the subject of consequence remains, but for the occurrence of the consequence, ownership is a condition, and here ownership is absent. So the oath should not remain. Answer: we are not speaking about the occurrence of the consequence, but about the survival of the oath. And the oath initially does not require ownership, because saying 'If I marry you, you are divorced' is valid even though the swearer does not own the power of divorce at that time. So when the inception of the oath does not require ownership, survival is even less likely to require it, because survival is easier than inception. Then there are two scenarios: (1) The condition occurs while in his ownership; e.g., he remarries the woman, then the condition occurs. (2) The condition occurs outside his ownership; e.g., before remarriage the condition occurs. In the first case, divorce occurs and the oath is completed. Divorce occurs because the condition (entering the house) occurred in ownership, so the consequence (divorce) which is attached to it also occurs. The oath is completed because the word 'inna' does not indicate repetition, so once the condition occurs, the oath is fulfilled. In the second case, the oath is completed because the condition occurred, but divorce does not occur because the subject is non-existent.
Source pages p. 336

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from al-Quduri's matn, expanded upon by the commentator. The principle: an oath of conditional divorce (ta'liq al-talaq) is not invalidated if the husband loses ownership of his wife (by a divorce or other means) after swearing but before the condition occurs. The reasoning is that the oath's survival depends on the survival of both the condition (the event) and the consequence (the divorce), not on current ownership. The condition is still possible, and the consequence still applies to the wife who exists as a legal subject. The commentator addresses an objection: if ownership is required for the divorce to take effect, how can the oath remain without ownership? The answer distinguishes between the inception of the oath (which can be made before marriage) and its continuation. Since an oath can be made when one does not yet own the power of divorce (e.g., 'If I marry you, you are divorced'), its survival does not require ownership either. Two scenarios follow: (a) if the condition occurs after remarriage (ownership regained), the divorce occurs; (b) if the condition occurs before remarriage (no ownership), the oath is fulfilled but no divorce takes effect because the wife is no longer a valid subject for divorce. This is a key distinction in Hanafi ta'liq law.

Key Terms
یمین (yamin): An oath, specifically a conditional divorce oath in this context, where the consequence is a divorce.
شرط (shart): The condition upon which the divorce is suspended, e.g., entering a house.
جزاء (jaza'): The consequence, i.e., the divorce itself, which occurs upon fulfillment of the condition.
ملک (mulk): Ownership, specifically the husband's right to divorce his wife (milk al-talaq).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man says to his wife, 'If you enter the house, you are divorced.' Then before she enters, he divorces her with a bain divorce. Later she re-enters the house. What is the Hanafi ruling?
A) The conditional divorce is void because he lost ownership.
B) The conditional oath remains; if she enters after remarriage, divorce occurs.
C) The conditional oath is invalid because the first divorce already occurred.
D) The conditional oath is fulfilled at the time of the first divorce.

Key Takeaway
A conditional divorce oath is not voided by loss of ownership; it remains in effect and can be triggered if the condition occurs while the wife is again under his ownership.
